 Here are the detailed steps to transform the input grid into its output grid, based on the overall pattern provided:

Transformation steps:

1. Determine the dimensions of the input grid and initialize an empty output grid of the same size.
2. Iterate through each object in the input grid and perform the following sub-steps:
   1. Extract the color, coordinates, and size of the current object.
   2. Apply the matrix transformation (rotation, scaling, shear, or reflection) to the object's coordinates, based on its size and position.
   3. Calculate the new position of the object based on the periodic boundary conditions determined by its color. This could involve wrapping the object around the edges of the grid if it reaches the boundaries.
   4. Update the output grid with the transformed object's coordinates.
3. Repeat steps 2a-2d until a stable configuration is reached, i.e., no further changes occur in the output grid.

Now, here are the specific transformations for each example:

Example\_1:
conditions:

* Objects with color 3 appear before objects with color 7.
* Each object has the same width but varying heights.
* There is a consistent spacing between objects of the same color.

transformation:

1. Initialize an empty output grid of size [10, 10].
2. For each object in the input grid, do the following:

a. If the object's color is 3, then shift its y-coordinate to the right by 1 unit.
b. If the object's color is 7, then shift its y-coordinate to the left by 1 unit.
c. Add the updated object's coordinates to the output grid.

Example\_2:

Same transformation as Example\_1, except with a larger number of objects and a slightly modified shifting rule:

1. If the object's color is 3, then shift its y-coordinate to the right by 1 unit.
2. If the object's color is 7, then shift its y-coordinate to the left by 1 unit, and move it down by 1 unit if it is located in row 1.

Example\_3:

In this example, objects alternate between colors 3 and 7, so the transformation shifts them horizontally based on their color:

1. Initialize an empty output grid of size [10, 10].
2. For each object in the input grid, do the following:

a. If the object's color is 3, then shift its x-coordinate to the left by 1 unit.
b. If the object's color is 7, then shift its x-coordinate to the right by 1 unit.
c. Add the updated object's coordinates to the output grid.

transformation\_steps:

2. Define a function that applies the appropriate transformation based on the conditions observed in the examples.
